[1mNAME[0m[m
       w - Show who is logged on and what they are doing.[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mw[0m [[4moptions[24m] [4muser[24m [...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mw[0m  displays  information  about the users currently on the machine, and[m
       their processes.  The header shows, in this order,  the  current  time,[m
       how  long  the  system  has  been running, how many users are currently[m
       logged on, and the system load averages for the past 1, 5, and 15  min‚Äê[m
       utes.[m
[m
       The  following entries are displayed for each user: login name, the tty[m
       name, the remote host, login time, idle time, JCPU, PCPU, and the  com‚Äê[m
       mand line of their current process.[m
[m
       The  JCPU  time  is the time used by all processes attached to the tty.[m
       It does not include past background jobs, but  does  include  currently[m
       running background jobs.[m
[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       time - run programs and summarize system resource usage[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mtime[0m   [ [1m-apqvV[0m ] [ [1m-f[0m [4mFORMAT[24m ] [ [1m-o[0m [4mFILE[24m ][m
              [ [1m--append[0m ] [ [1m--verbose[0m ] [ [1m--quiet[0m ] [ [1m--portability[0m ][m
              [ [1m--format=[0m[4mFORMAT[24m ] [ [1m--output=[0m[4mFILE[24m ] [ [1m--version[0m ][m
              [ [1m--help[0m ] [4mCOMMAND[24m [ [4mARGS[24m ][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mtime[0m run the program [4mCOMMAND[24m with any given arguments [4mARG...[24m.  When[m
       [4mCOMMAND[24m finishes, [1mtime[0m displays information about resources used by[m
       [4mCOMMAND[24m (on the standard error output, by default).  If [4mCOMMAND[24m exits[m
       with non-zero status, [1mtime[0m displays a warning message and the exit[m
       status.[m
[m
       [1mtime[0m determines which information to display about the resources used[m
       by the [4mCOMMAND[24m from the string [4mFORMAT[24m.  If no format is specified on[m
       the command line, but the [1mTIME[0m environment variable is set, its value[m
       is used as the format.  Otherwise, a default format built into [1mtime[0m is[m
       used.[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       df - report file system disk space usage[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mdf[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       This  manual  page  documents  the  GNU version of [1mdf[0m.  [1mdf[0m displays the[m
       amount of disk space available on the file system containing each  file[m
       name  argument.   If  no file name is given, the space available on all[m
       currently mounted file systems is shown.  Disk space  is  shown  in  1K[m
       blocks  by  default, unless the environment variable POSIXLY_CORRECT is[m
       set, in which case 512-byte blocks are used.[m
[m
       If an argument is the absolute file name of a disk device node contain‚Äê[m
       ing  a  mounted  file system, [1mdf[0m shows the space available on that file[m
       system rather than on the file system containing the device node.  This[m
       version  of  [1mdf[0m  cannot show the space available on unmounted file sys‚Äê[m
       tems, because on most kinds of systems  doing  so  requires  very  non‚Äê[m
       portable intimate knowledge of file system structures.[m
[m

df
[0mGives an overview of the filesystem disk space usage.More information: https://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/df.

 - [23;22;24;25;32mDisplay all filesystems and their disk usage:

[1mNAME[0m[m
       bash - GNU Bourne-Again SHell[m

[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mBash[0m  is  an  [1msh[0m-compatible  command language interpreter that executes[m
       commands read from the standard input or from a file.  [1mBash[0m also incor‚Äê[m
       porates useful features from the [4mKorn[24m and [4mC[24m shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  is  intended  to  be a conformant implementation of the Shell and[m
       Utilities portion  of  the  IEEE  POSIX  specification  (IEEE  Standard[m
       1003.1).  [1mBash[0m can be configured to be POSIX-conformant by default.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       All of the single-character shell options documented in the description[m
       of the [1mset[0m builtin command, including [1m-o[0m, can be used as  options  when[m

bash
[0mBourne-Again SHell, an sh-compatible command-line interpreter.See also histexpand for history expansion.More information: https://gnu.org/software/bash/.

 - [23;22;24;25;32mStart an interactive shell session:

 - [23;22;24;25;32mExecute a command and then exit:

 - [23;22;24;25;32mExecute a script:

[0m

[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=CHMOD(1)                         User Commands                        CHMOD(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       chmod - change file mode bits[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mchmod[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4mMODE[24m[[4m,MODE[24m]... [4mFILE[24m...[m
       [1mchmod[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4mOCTAL-MODE[24m [4mFILE[24m...[m
       [1mchmod[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--reference=RFILE[24m [4mFILE[24m...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       This manual page documents the GNU version of [1mchmod[0m.  [1mchmod[0m changes the[m
       file mode bits of each given file according to [4mmode[24m, which can  be  ei‚Äê[m
       ther  a  symbolic representation of changes to make, or an octal number[m
       representing the bit pattern for the new mode bits.[m
[m
       The format of a symbolic mode is  [[1mugoa[0m...][[[1m-+=[0m][[4mperms[24m...]...],  where[m
       [4mperms[24m  is  either zero or more letters from the set [1mrwxXst[0m, or a single[m
       letter from the set [1mugo[0m.  Multiple symbolic modes can be  given,  sepa‚Äê[m
       rated by commas.[m
[m
       A  combination  of the letters [1mugoa[0m controls which users' access to the[m
       file will be changed: the user who owns it  ([1mu[0m),  other  users  in  the[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       file's group ([1mg[0m), other users not in the file's group ([1mo[0m), or all users[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       ([1ma[0m).  If none of these are given, the effect is as if ([1ma[0m)  were  given,[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       but bits that are set in the umask are not affected.[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The  operator  [1m+[0m  causes the selected file mode bits to be added to the[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       existing file mode bits of each file; [1m-[0m causes them to be removed;  and[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m=[0m causes them to be added and causes unmentioned bits to be removed ex‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       cept that a directory's unmentioned set user and group ID bits are  not[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       affected.[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The  letters  [1mrwxXst[0m select file mode bits for the affected users: read[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 12 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       ([1mr[0m), write ([1mw[0m), execute (or search for directories) ([1mx[0m), execute/search[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       only  if  the file is a directory or already has execute permission for[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       some user ([1mX[0m), set user or group ID on execution ([1ms[0m), restricted  dele‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       tion  flag or sticky bit ([1mt[0m).  Instead of one or more of these letters,[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 16 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       you can specify exactly one of the letters [1mugo[0m: the permissions granted[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       to  the  user  who  owns the file ([1mu[0m), the permissions granted to other[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       users who are members of the file's  group  ([1mg[0m),  and  the  permissions[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       granted  to  users  that are in neither of the two preceding categories[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       ([1mo[0m).[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       A numeric mode is from one to  four  octal  digits  (0-7),  derived  by[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 23 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       adding up the bits with values 4, 2, and 1.  Omitted digits are assumed[m
[7m Manual page chmod(1) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       to be leading zeros.  The first digit selects the set user ID  (4)  and[m

chmod
[0mChange the access permissions of a file or directory.More information: https://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/chmod.

 - [23;22;24;25;32mGive the [u]ser who owns a file the right to e[x]ecute it:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod u+x {{file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mGive the [u]ser rights to [r]ead and [w]rite to a file/directory:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod u+rw {{file_or_directory}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mRemove e[x]ecutable rights from the [g]roup:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod g-x {{file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mGive [a]ll users rights to [r]ead and e[x]ecute:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod a+rx {{file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mGive [o]thers (not in the file owner's group) the same rights as the [g]roup:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod o=g {{file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mRemove all rights from [o]thers:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod o= {{file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mChange permissions recursively giving [g]roup and [o]thers the ability to [w]rite:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod -R g+w,o+w {{directory}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mRecursively give [a]ll users [r]ead permissions to files and e[X]ecute permissions to sub-directories within a directory:
[23;22;24;25;33m   chmod -R a+rX {{directory}}

[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=PS(1)                            User Commands                           PS(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       ps - report a snapshot of the current processes.[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mps[0m [[4moptions[24m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mps[0m displays information about a selection of the active processes.  If[m
       you want a repetitive update of the selection and the displayed[m
       information, use [4mtop[24m(1) instead.[m
[m
       This version of [1mps[0m accepts several kinds of options:[m
[m
       1   UNIX options, which may be grouped and must be preceded by a dash.[m
       2   BSD options, which may be grouped and must not be used with a dash.[m
       3   GNU long options, which are preceded by two dashes.[m
[m
       Options of different types may be freely mixed, but conflicts can[m
       appear.  There are some synonymous options, which are functionally[m
       identical, due to the many standards and [1mps[0m implementations that this[m
       [1mps[0m is compatible with.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       Note that "[1mps[0m [1m-aux[0m" is distinct from "[1mps[0m [1maux[0m".  The POSIX and UNIX[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       standards require that "[1mps[0m [1m-aux[0m" print all processes owned by a user[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       named "x", as well as printing all processes that would be selected by[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       the [1m-a[0m option.  If the user named "x" does not exist, this [1mps[0m may[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       interpret the command as "[1mps[0m [1maux[0m" instead and print a warning.  This[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       behavior is intended to aid in transitioning old scripts and habits.[m
[7m Manual page ps(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       It is fragile, subject to change, and thus should not be relied upon.[m

]0;kamal@kamal-Inspiron-3593: ~/Desktop/OS[01;32mkamal@kamal-Inspiron-3593[00m:[01;34m~/Desktop/OS[00m$ ps [K[K[Kman kill[Kl
[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=KILL(1)                          User Commands                         KILL(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       kill - send a signal to a process[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mkill[0m [options] <pid> [...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The  default  signal  for kill is TERM.  Use [1m-l[0m or [1m-L[0m to list available[m
       signals.  Particularly useful signals include  HUP,  INT,  KILL,  STOP,[m
       CONT,  and  0.   Alternate  signals may be specified in three ways: [1m-9[0m,[m
       [1m-SIGKILL[0m or [1m-KILL[0m.  Negative PID values may be  used  to  choose  whole[m
       process  groups; see the PGID column in ps command output.  A PID of [1m-1[0m[m
       is special; it indicates all processes except the kill  process  itself[m
       and init.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m<pid>[0m [1m[...][0m[m
              Send signal to every <pid> listed.[m
[m
       [1m-<signal>[0m[m
       [1m-s[0m [1m<signal>[0m[m
[7m Manual page kill(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m--signal[0m [1m<signal>[0m[m
[7m Manual page kill(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Specify  the  [1msignal[0m to be sent.  The signal can be specified by[m
[7m Manual page kill(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              using name or number.  The behavior of signals is  explained  in[m
[7m Manual page kill(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              [1msignal[0m(7) manual page.[m
[7m Manual page kill(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m

[7m Manual page kill(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              List  signal  names.   This  option has optional argument, which[m

kill
[0mSends a signal to a process, usually related to stopping the process.All signals except for SIGKILL and SIGSTOP can be intercepted by the process to perform a clean exit.More information: https://manned.org/kill.

 - [23;22;24;25;32mTerminate a program using the default SIGTERM (terminate) signal:
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill {{process_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mList available signal names (to be used without the SIG prefix):
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -l
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mTerminate a background job:
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill %{{job_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mTerminate a program using the SIGHUP (hang up) signal. Many daemons will reload instead of terminating:
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -{{1|HUP}} {{process_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mTerminate a program using the SIGINT (interrupt) signal. This is typically initiated by the user pressing Ctrl + C:
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -{{2|INT}} {{process_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSignal the operating system to immediately terminate a program (which gets no chance to capture the signal):
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -{{9|KILL}} {{process_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSignal the operating system to pause a program until a SIGCONT ("continue") signal is received:
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -{{17|STOP}} {{process_id}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSend a SIGUSR1 signal to all processes with the given GID (group id):
[23;22;24;25;33m   kill -{{SIGUSR1}} -{{group_id}}

[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=GREP(1)                          User Commands                         GREP(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       grep, egrep, fgrep, rgrep - print lines that match patterns[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTION[24m...] [4mPATTERNS[24m [[4mFILE[24m...][m
       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTION[24m...] [1m-e[0m [4mPATTERNS[24m ... [[4mFILE[24m...][m
       [1mgrep[0m [[4mOPTION[24m...] [1m-f[0m [4mPATTERN_FILE[24m ... [[4mFILE[24m...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mgrep[0m  searches  for  [4mPATTERNS[24m  in  each  [4mFILE[24m.  [4mPATTERNS[24m is one or more[m
       patterns separated by newline characters, and  [1mgrep[0m  prints  each  line[m
       that  matches a pattern.  Typically [4mPATTERNS[24m should be quoted when [1mgrep[0m[m
       is used in a shell command.[m
[m
       A [4mFILE[24m of ‚Äú[1m-[0m‚Äù  stands  for  standard  input.   If  no  [4mFILE[24m  is  given,[m
       recursive  searches  examine  the  working  directory, and nonrecursive[m
       searches read standard input.[m
[m
       In addition, the variant programs [1megrep[0m, [1mfgrep[0m and [1mrgrep[0m are  the  same[m
       as  [1mgrep[0m [1m-E[0m,  [1mgrep[0m [1m-F[0m,  and  [1mgrep[0m [1m-r[0m, respectively.  These variants are[m
       deprecated, but are provided for backward compatibility.[m

grep
[0mFind patterns in files using regular expressions.More information: https://www.gnu.org/software/grep/manual/grep.html.

 - [23;22;24;25;32mSearch for a pattern within a file:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSearch for an exact string (disables regular expressions):
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --fixed-strings "{{exact_string}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSearch for a pattern in all files recursively in a directory, showing line numbers of matches, ignoring binary files:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --recursive --line-number --binary-files={{without-match}} "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/directory}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mUse extended regular expressions (supports ?, +, {}, () and |), in case-insensitive mode:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --extended-regexp --ignore-case "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mPrint 3 lines of context around, before, or after each match:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --{{context|before-context|after-context}}={{3}} "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mPrint file name and line number for each match:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --with-filename --line-number "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSearch for lines matching a pattern, printing only the matched text:
[23;22;24;25;33m   grep --only-matching "{{search_pattern}}" {{path/to/file}}
[0m
 - [23;22;24;25;32mSearch stdin for lines that do not match a pattern:
[23;22;24;25;33m   cat {{path/to/file}} | grep --invert-match "{{search_pattern}}"
